    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200953541?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bert Carson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bert Carson" href="/user/show/4916985-bert-carson">Bert Carson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200953541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8191496151576563704">Like all of Diehl's books, Primal Fear is outstanding. A week after it was published I was reading it on a flight from Atlanta to San Francisco. First class was almost empty and I was the only one awake when the steward knelt down beside my seat and whispered, "I noticed the book you are reading. It's obvious you are either a psychologist or a psychiatrist." Before I could correct him, he blurted out, "I have a primal fear of flying." I listened to his entire story, carefully closing the book an</span>
  <span id="freeText8191496151576563704" style="display:none">Like all of Diehl's books, Primal Fear is outstanding. A week after it was published I was reading it on a flight from Atlanta to San Francisco. First class was almost empty and I was the only one awake when the steward knelt down beside my seat and whispered, "I noticed the book you are reading. It's obvious you are either a psychologist or a psychiatrist." Before I could correct him, he blurted out, "I have a primal fear of flying." I listened to his entire story, carefully closing the book and sliding it under my blanket so he wouldn't discover that it was a novel. When he was done I gave him some free "professional advise" which seemed to thrill him. I slipped the book into my brief case and got back to reading it at the hotel. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_950549366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950549366" />
    <a title="Supratim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21432277-supratim"><img alt="Supratim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560446219p2/21432277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950549366?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Supratim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Supratim" href="/user/show/21432277-supratim">Supratim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21432277-supratim?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950549366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4436219350004548455">A worthy read for the Goodreads Mystery and Thriller Week!!<br/><br/>This is my first book by the author, and I must say I did enjoy reading the novel: a psychological thriller-cum- courtroom drama.<br/><br/>In Chicago, an archbishop – called the “Saint of Lakeview Drive” has been brutalized and a young man, Aaron Stampler, has been arrested from the scene of crime with the murder weapon. The evidence points to Aaron’s guilt, and he is facing capital punishment.<br/><br/>Now we are introduced to Martin aka Marty Vail, ex-arm</span>
  <span id="freeText4436219350004548455" style="display:none">A worthy read for the Goodreads Mystery and Thriller Week!!<br /><br />This is my first book by the author, and I must say I did enjoy reading the novel: a psychological thriller-cum- courtroom drama.<br /><br />In Chicago, an archbishop – called the “Saint of Lakeview Drive” has been brutalized and a young man, Aaron Stampler, has been arrested from the scene of crime with the murder weapon. The evidence points to Aaron’s guilt, and he is facing capital punishment.<br /><br />Now we are introduced to Martin aka Marty Vail, ex-army lawyer turned defense counselor– an irreverent and a bit shabby man. But, yes of course, a brilliant and uncompromising lawyer who gets what he wants – hated by the prosecutors and judges. He has successfully sued the city, county and state for 1.6 million dollars for his low life client. In order to teach Vail a lesson and some humility, Judge Hangin’ Harry Shoats makes him take Aaron’s case.<br /><br />Pitted against Vail, is prosecutor Jane Venable – as uncompromising as Vail himself. She is assisted by the efficient Lt. Stenner, nicknamed the Icicle, and his team of seasoned professionals. <br /><br />What I liked about the book is that Vail is not portrayed as a “one-man-army”. Instead he is helped by a pretty great team– a highly competent secretary, an ex-boxer turned law student to help with the investigation and an ex-judge as a mentor. They would be joined by a young and attractive psychiatrist, and, you have guessed it right – something would develop between her and Vail. <br />I am not going into the details of the story, but would caution you that you would come across some pretty perverse and devious stuff. I enjoyed some of the dialogues and the legal skills of Counselor Vail. <br /><br />Mid way or a little past the mid way, you can easily guess what is coming. But, still it is quite fun to read.<br /><br />This might not be a great piece of literature, but it never claimed to be one. The book is a thriller which promised to provide thrills and suspense – and this it did quite well.<br /><br />I am giving the book a rating of 3.5, which I am rounding off to 4!<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4436219350004548455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7761269329463308950" style="display:none">Those of you who have seen the excellent movie made from this book will have a pretty good idea where it winds up. I saw the movie long before getting the book, so the ending wasn’t a huge surprise, and I found the book to be quite interesting with intriguing characters:<br /><br />-Vail, the successful lawyer dragged into a case he didn't want because the judge wants to hand him a sure loss as punishment for Vails successful suit against the city ;<br />- Mollie, the young psychologist who wanted to be a biologist until her brother returned from Vietnam slowly entering a state of catatonia;<br />-Rebecca, Stempler’s former teacher who taught in a one-room schoolhouse and saw him as one of her few success stories, the boy who didn’t go down in the hole; <br />-the brilliant prosecutor who didn’t want the case either but was dragged into it as her last case before she left the D.A.’s office;<br />-Goodman, the sensitive P.I. working on his law degree, a former boxer whose career disintegrated when he smashed his hand;<br />and Aaron Stempler, genius IQ who could read Latin and devoured every book he could get his hands on who is accused of the brutal murder of Catholic Archbishop Rushmon who had befriended him. The evidence against Aaron is overwhelming. <br />-And then there’s Roy.<br /><br />First rate legal novel. The courtroom scenes are magnificent.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer478819514088599758">I will never forget when I was finishing this book. I was relaxing after a day at work with the last 50 pages, enjoying the way Diehl was wrapping up the story. I got to the last few pages and was so completely surprised by the twist Diehl put into the story that I sat bolt upright, said basically what the heck (and no, not I didn't actually use that mild of an explicative) and instantly turned back those pages to make sure I wasn't hallucinating what I had just read.   <span id="freeText478819514088599758" style="display:none">I will never forget when I was finishing this book. I was relaxing after a day at work with the last 50 pages, enjoying the way Diehl was wrapping up the story. I got to the last few pages and was so completely surprised by the twist Diehl put into the story that I sat bolt upright, said basically what the heck (and no, not I didn't actually use that mild of an explicative) and instantly turned back those pages to make sure I wasn't hallucinating what I had just read. I don't get a lot of what the heck just happened moments when I read books these days, but this one supplied one of the best I've ever had. Kudos to Diehl for baiting a good hook.</span>

<div id="review_136261431" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136261431" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136261431?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749336653" href="/book/show/969193.Primal_Fear">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of psychological and legal thrillers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=saw-movie">saw-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=thriller-mystery-suspense">thriller-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136261431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3651966227888798628">Although I saw the movie adaptation with Richard Gere and Edward Norton, I wanted to read this book because I was curious how the author would present his story on paper. It turned out that William Diehl did a great job at mixing psychological suspense with legal coutroom drama.<br/><br/>Aaaron Stampler is accused of murdering Archbishop Richard Rushman - in fact police find him near the scene of the murder - hiding in a confessional, soaked with blood and gripping the murder weapon. Defense attorney Mart</span>
  <span id="freeText3651966227888798628" style="display:none">Although I saw the movie adaptation with Richard Gere and Edward Norton, I wanted to read this book because I was curious how the author would present his story on paper. It turned out that William Diehl did a great job at mixing psychological suspense with legal coutroom drama.<br /><br />Aaaron Stampler is accused of murdering Archbishop Richard Rushman - in fact police find him near the scene of the murder - hiding in a confessional, soaked with blood and gripping the murder weapon. Defense attorney Martin Vail is forced to take Stampler's case pro-bono - Vail has recently won a case against the city, county and the state police, which all hope that this case will humiliate and destroy him.<br /><br />I'm not a big mystery or thriller reader - In fact I tend to avoid them. Novels in these genres usually run in series, with the same protagonist - usually a detective or a lawyer. However, I was impressed by the film which was made from this novel and I'm glad I decided to give it a go.<br /><br />Martin Vail's characters is rich and vivid - if Gordon Gekko went to law school he'll be him. His supporting team is not shabby either - the private investigator Tommy Goodman, an ex-boxer who digs nasty details about the case and the murdered Bishop.Psychologist Molly Arrington analyses Aaron and is instrumental in bringing facts that Vail can use in court.<br /><br />However, the real diamond here is the character of Aaron Stampler, an angelic faced, mild boy. A complex character, Aaron is seemingly inscrutable and denies comitting the murder. As Vail races against time to form a defense for his client, the novel drastically increases the level of suspense which literally explodes in the final coutroom scene, and - what's incredible - offers a conclusion that imprints itself in the mind of the reader and makes him think about what he has just read.<br />A classic novel in the genre, <i>Primal Fear</i> offers much more than the rest of the lot and is a great fun to read. Recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3651966227888798628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_209086029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209086029" />
    <a title="Tiara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2426502-tiara"><img alt="Tiara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245188991p2/2426502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209086029?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tiara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tiara" href="/user/show/2426502-tiara">Tiara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2426502-tiara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2426502-tiara?shelf=book-turned-media-and-vice-versa">book-turned-media-and-vice-versa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2426502-tiara?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller-noir">crime-mystery-thriller-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209086029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13497941364418850503">Aaron Stampler is found in a confessional booth holding a knife, proclaiming his innocence, after someone killed the revered Bishop of the city. Martin Vail, a quick-witted lawyer who isn't afraid to leap before he looks, is basically coerced into defending the young man who appears guilty in every sense of the word. Every politician in the city seems to have a vendetta against Vail and looks foward to seeing him lose the case.<br/><br/>Liked the movie. Loved the book. As with most book-to-movie adaptatio</span>
  <span id="freeText13497941364418850503" style="display:none">Aaron Stampler is found in a confessional booth holding a knife, proclaiming his innocence, after someone killed the revered Bishop of the city. Martin Vail, a quick-witted lawyer who isn't afraid to leap before he looks, is basically coerced into defending the young man who appears guilty in every sense of the word. Every politician in the city seems to have a vendetta against Vail and looks foward to seeing him lose the case.<br /><br />Liked the movie. Loved the book. As with most book-to-movie adaptations, the book was better. Unlike his movie persona, Vail isn't cool, well-dressed sauveness that Richard Gere presented. The Vail in the book is a man who isn't overly concerned about his personal appearance, and he isn't afraid to grab at straws, and he makes lawyers tremble just at the mention of his name. <br /><br />The book also provided more insight on Aaron. You get a taste of his childhood and find out more about what molded him. In the book, Aaron is a genius, despite the accent and his angelic appearance. His childhood wasn't the best thing, and he's even described as being able to detach himself from tragedies. Is that enough to make him a killer? Is he mentally stable?<br /><br />I'm sure by now, most people have heard about the twist, but that doesn't take the impact away from reading it for yourself. I read the "twist" over and over again, even though I've seen the movie and knew what to expect. A first-rate legal thriller. I can't wait to read the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13497941364418850503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1183129684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183129684" />
    <a title="Andjela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14293227-andjela"><img alt="Andjela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504561801p2/14293227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183129684?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andjela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andjela" href="/user/show/14293227-andjela">Andjela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18908778-primal-fear">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183129684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4803483291170457377">A masterfully crafted novel. The writing is superb, the attention to detail magnificent and the story itself is particularly thrilling and interesting. I watched the movie a few years back, so I knew the ending. Even with a huge spoiler like that, I thoroughly enjoyed this book and it was as gripping and suspenseful as it would be if I had no clue about the resolution of the story. I really enjoyed Diehl's writing style, and I can't wait to get my hands on some of the other books he wrote.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1014326115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1014326115" />
    <a title="Joe  Noir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16399833-joe-noir"><img alt="Joe  Noir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358100499p2/16399833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1014326115?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe  Noir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe  Noir" href="/user/show/16399833-joe-noir">Joe  Noir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1014326115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3259836463124439006">Unlike <u>Sharky’s Machine</u> (also by William Diehl) in which the good guys obviously wore the white hats, and the bad guys obviously wore the black hats, this novel, <u>Primal Fear</u>, is all shades of gray…and blood red.<br/><br/>A high profile defense attorney who has never lost a case is assigned to defend, pro bono, the altar boy accused of butchering the city’s most popular archbishop. The bishop was found in pieces, literally, in his residence and the accused was found covered in the bishop’s blood, hiding in</span>
  <span id="freeText3259836463124439006" style="display:none">Unlike <u>Sharky’s Machine</u> (also by William Diehl) in which the good guys obviously wore the white hats, and the bad guys obviously wore the black hats, this novel, <u>Primal Fear</u>, is all shades of gray…and blood red.<br /><br />A high profile defense attorney who has never lost a case is assigned to defend, pro bono, the altar boy accused of butchering the city’s most popular archbishop. The bishop was found in pieces, literally, in his residence and the accused was found covered in the bishop’s blood, hiding in a confessional in the adjacent church, holding the murder weapon. It’s considered a slam dunk for the prosecution. Movers and shakers want to see this kid ride the electric chair.<br /><br />The defense attorney, Martin Vail, is assigned this case by the sitting judge as payback. Vail recently won a settlement from the city and state for several million dollars on behalf of a client. The powers that be think this new case will be a major loss for Vail. The prosecutor, Jane Venable, and Vail have a history. She was about to leave the prosecutor’s office for private practice, and was “persuaded” to stay long enough to handle the “slam dunk” case. <br /><br />Watching Vail and his team prepare for trial is fascinating. Each step along the way is professional and painstaking. One hopes real life legal defense teams are this good (<u>Sharky's Machine</u> was also about a good team working well together). Additional bodies are found, and secret messages are found on the bodies. More evidence and witnesses are found. A defense strategy begins to come together.<br /><br />As the trial starts, Vail begins to chip away at the prosecution’s case…and maybe it’s not such a “slam dunk” after all.<br /><br />This novel raises a number of questions about the way the justice system works. Actual innocence or guilt is sometimes lost in the process of winning or losing. People are used as chess pieces in a game of life or death. Each character is well drawn and fully developed. Martin Vail is largely a very likable person, but has ruthless qualities. Just as with Michael Connelly’s <u>The Fifth Witness</u>, I find the most frightening thing is the thought of being an innocent person accused in the justice system. Most of us would not have the financial resources to mount a successful defense, or hire the very best attorneys.<br /><br />I have to tell you, I saw two major plot twists in this novel coming from early on in the book; and though they were handled extremely well by the author, I was disappointed as they seemed obvious to me. Make no mistake, this is still a thumping good read, difficult to put down, and very entertaining. If you might like a legal thriller combined with psychological horror, this could be the book for you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3259836463124439006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1674091254" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1674091254" />
    <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews"><img alt="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346883958p2/12558730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674091254?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews">M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=legal">legal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674091254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8929276933245178188">For a book that had so much hype, I have to say that I am rather disappointed. Most of the book was engaging, and I was prepared to give it a higher rating. However, I was hit with the disappointment one has when something starts, and goes on with plenty of promise, only to fizzle out in the end... which is exactly what happened with this book. The last court scene felt like the author had just gotten bored of his work and decided to just wrap things up quickly. I realize there are a couple more</span>
  <span id="freeText8929276933245178188" style="display:none">For a book that had so much hype, I have to say that I am rather disappointed. Most of the book was engaging, and I was prepared to give it a higher rating. However, I was hit with the disappointment one has when something starts, and goes on with plenty of promise, only to fizzle out in the end... which is exactly what happened with this book. The last court scene felt like the author had just gotten bored of his work and decided to just wrap things up quickly. I realize there are a couple more books after this one, but it... just did not click for me. The very last chapter/scene just made it even worse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8929276933245178188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1437795809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437795809" />

<span id="freeTextContainer9700297516588947639">Thought provoking <br/><br/>A Bishop with an eminent standing in the local community is sadistically murdered by a teenager who was under his care, to the point that beyond the large amount of mortal wounds inflicted all over his body, his genital organs end up stuffed in his mouth .The potential perpetrator is a teenager suffering from a multiple personality disorder. Was he or his alter ego ?, is he accountable if his alter ego has done it ?, is multiple personality disorder a recognized mental disease </span>
  <span id="freeText9700297516588947639" style="display:none">Thought provoking <br /><br />A Bishop with an eminent standing in the local community is sadistically murdered by a teenager who was under his care, to the point that beyond the large amount of mortal wounds inflicted all over his body, his genital organs end up stuffed in his mouth .The potential perpetrator is a teenager suffering from a multiple personality disorder. Was he or his alter ego ?, is he accountable if his alter ego has done it ?, is multiple personality disorder a recognized mental disease ?, is the physical evidence found in the room where the crime took place good enough beyond reasonable doubt to nail the accused and punish him with the electric chair ?..., Is this situation real or is the accused actually faking the disorder? Was the murder premeditated ? Who is the Bishop indeed ?<br />Legal psycho thriller, with two great caracter developments, Vail,the flamboyant fiery defense attorney who is defending the teenager pro bono, and Aaron the defendant, who acts as an individual with two turning personalities, Aaron the gifted innocent hilbilly boy, and Roy the mean sadistic beast who cannot tell good from evil. <br />Then second half of the book where the ardent criminal trial unfolds, featuring lost of interesting questioning, is far more interesting and better writtten that the first half of the book which encompasses the heinous criminal act and ensuing investigation, the ending holds a great surprise, making the whole book worth reading. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9700297516588947639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10606501997885622831">First and best in a series, followed by "Show Of Evil" and "Reign In Hell."<br/><br/>Also a great film starring Richard Gere and Edward Norton in his debut role.<br/><br/>The city of Chicago is shocked when their "saint of Lakeview Drive," Archbishop Richard Bernard Rushman, is brutally murdered in his own rectory. Nineteen year old Aaron Stampler is found crouched in a church confessional, covered in the bishop's blood, mumbling, "Didn't do it, Mama."<br/><br/>Attorney Martin Vail is known for his rough tactics as well as h</span>
  <span id="freeText10606501997885622831" style="display:none">First and best in a series, followed by "Show Of Evil" and "Reign In Hell."<br /><br />Also a great film starring Richard Gere and Edward Norton in his debut role.<br /><br />The city of Chicago is shocked when their "saint of Lakeview Drive," Archbishop Richard Bernard Rushman, is brutally murdered in his own rectory. Nineteen year old Aaron Stampler is found crouched in a church confessional, covered in the bishop's blood, mumbling, "Didn't do it, Mama."<br /><br />Attorney Martin Vail is known for his rough tactics as well as his brilliant performances in the courtroom. He is hated by every prosecutor in the city. Vail loves and lives the law. Vail is forced to defend Aaron Stampler as sort of a "slap on the wrist." Aaron's Appalachian mountain accent and angelic appearance is only the beginning to a great defense.<br /><br />Author William Diehl hits the jackpot with this tale of murder and suspense. His characters are so real in their descriptions and dialog, it's easy to love and/or hate them. Great book to recommend (if you haven't already seen the movie).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10606501997885622831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12668913750155193207">Excellent writing and some of the best characters I've met.<br/>I've seen the movie years ago but didn't expect the book to be as good, if not better. Usually that is the case but something at the back of my mind told me not to get my hopes up. I was proven wrong, the book revealed to me one of my new favourite genres of writing: courtroom thriller.<br/>The text is easy to read, the jargon isn't too difficult and the switch between past and present events, or descriptions of characters backrounds, works w</span>
  <span id="freeText12668913750155193207" style="display:none">Excellent writing and some of the best characters I've met.<br />I've seen the movie years ago but didn't expect the book to be as good, if not better. Usually that is the case but something at the back of my mind told me not to get my hopes up. I was proven wrong, the book revealed to me one of my new favourite genres of writing: courtroom thriller.<br />The text is easy to read, the jargon isn't too difficult and the switch between past and present events, or descriptions of characters backrounds, works well.<br />I liked Vail and Naomi. Also, Aaron's character was excellent.<br />By the way, it suddenly strikes me odd how much sex there was in this book in relation to how needless it was. I mean, it could have easily been left out.<br />Anyway, the plot is great and I liked how Diehl worked his way to the end. Also, the fact that there were so many characters didn't bother me at all, when it usually does. I often find it hard to keep up and forget who was who but Diehl is just so good, it was easy to follow. I guess it <i>is&gt; alot to do with the talent of the author. <br />Overall a very enjoyable experience, Diehl is good!</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3076680935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1313372512008271858">Rating this book was so conflicting - about half of it is unnecessary background and conversation that's completely unrelated to the story, and I was able to guess the general ending about 1/4 of the way in. However, there was a small twist at the end that took me by surprise, and for that alone I was able to bump it up to 3 stars. Perhaps it's because I read too many mysteries, but if there's one thing I've learned for sure after reading Primal Fear, A Great Deliverance, and Dr. Jekyll and Mr. </span>
  <span id="freeText1313372512008271858" style="display:none">Rating this book was so conflicting - about half of it is unnecessary background and conversation that's completely unrelated to the story, and I was able to guess the general ending about 1/4 of the way in. However, there was a small twist at the end that took me by surprise, and for that alone I was able to bump it up to 3 stars. Perhaps it's because I read too many mysteries, but if there's one thing I've learned for sure after reading Primal Fear, A Great Deliverance, and Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde, it's that thrillers from the 1900s simply won't be very thrilling imo - as the themes all fall into the same categories. Nonetheless, a great story for its time.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10082035677614905638"><i>
  <b>I an't gonna forget this...Never in this life.</b>
</i><br/><br/>This is the kind of book you want all your friends to read. Afterwards, you hope you will sit down and discuss. None of that happened. That is not very pleasant. Anyway, that does not change the fact that it is a great book. Very relevant. I quickly rushed to check who Mr. William Diehl is? I thought he was either a lawyer or psychiatrist. Surprisingly, he was none of that. It is the type that you literally cannot lift your head from. Patience my</span>
  <span id="freeText10082035677614905638" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>I an't gonna forget this...Never in this life.</b>
</i><br /><br />This is the kind of book you want all your friends to read. Afterwards, you hope you will sit down and discuss. None of that happened. That is not very pleasant. Anyway, that does not change the fact that it is a great book. Very relevant. I quickly rushed to check who Mr. William Diehl is? I thought he was either a lawyer or psychiatrist. Surprisingly, he was none of that. It is the type that you literally cannot lift your head from. Patience my friend, patience and you will enjoy this one.<br /><br />Marty Vail the hot shot lawyer. He has tried a handful of cases with great success. Until he is appointed to represented Aaron. Is it time for him to swallow his pride? When he accepted to take that case, everyone including himself thought that he was digging his own grave. That case was an 'open-and-shut' case for the prosecution. Was his cockiness going to be the end of him or will it result in his greatest courtroom success in the course of his career?<br /><br />Aaron suffered from a mental disorder known as multiple or split personality disorder. There was Aaron and Roy in the same body. Aaron is the polite genius while Roy is the psychopath who has killed a number of people. Fortunately, with the help of his team he was able to overcome all the difficult obstacles and unearth all the grueling secrets. He found himself holding all the aces in the deck. Once he started running, he could not help it. He was like a dog with his tail on fire. Only that he did not have a tail on fire but one that was winning and winning big. He fought gallantly for his client Aaron. He defended him with a heroism which every young advocate would quickly be proud of and love to emulate. He fought prosecutors, police investigators, and the selfish politicians who were involved in this case.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_342207678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342207678" />
    <a title="Sully (thysaltymar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9986049-sully-thysaltymar"><img alt="Sully (thysaltymar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600734096p2/9986049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342207678?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sully (thysaltymar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sully (thysaltymar)" href="/user/show/9986049-sully-thysaltymar">Sully (thysaltymar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9986049-sully-thysaltymar?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342207678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13097594352191025523">This novel is not just another court-room drama, William Diehl created a bad-ass lawyer that contradicts with John Grisham lawyers (the conscience-loving lawyers).<br/> <br/>At first, you would think the story is quite predictable for the reason that the case seems rather clear: an altar boy running away from the home of the bishop where he's killed (scenario: a bishop with blood all over his clothes). No doubt that you would think of something like, 'he absolutely did it! Case closed!' However, the first</span>
  <span id="freeText13097594352191025523" style="display:none">This novel is not just another court-room drama, William Diehl created a bad-ass lawyer that contradicts with John Grisham lawyers (the conscience-loving lawyers).<br /> <br />At first, you would think the story is quite predictable for the reason that the case seems rather clear: an altar boy running away from the home of the bishop where he's killed (scenario: a bishop with blood all over his clothes). No doubt that you would think of something like, 'he absolutely did it! Case closed!' However, the first interesting twist in the novel appeared in the next chapter: The boy was caught and it's proved that he was at the murder scene but then he can't remember anything about the brutal murder, because at that exact moment he had a blackout. Now, Martain Vail is convinced that there was a third person at the Bishop's house. That third person must have killed the bishop, the boy's innocent. Now, Martin Vail's job is to prove the third man theory in the court room, but just as he thought that it would be that easy and while the legal process comes nearer to the end, new evidences came into the picture which make everything a lot clearer and difficult but more interesting.<br /><br />OVER-ALL, THIS BOOK HAS INTERESTING CHARACTERS, STORY AND TWISTS! AWESOME READ (although I love Grisham better)!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13097594352191025523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer637570019&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer637570019" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1614168014694217239">Marty Vail and the Psychopath. Bad boy lawyer Vail jams it up the governments ass sideways in a settlement, and is repaid by having to defend the accused in a viscous murder trial pro bono. As he peels the onion on Aaron Stampler, he finds that the boy is harboring deep psychological issues and upon further investigation finds that Aaron has a split personality, and that his alter ego is a satanic murderer. Facing the state that wants his client fried, Vail prepares and elaborate ruse to have th</span>
  <span id="freeText1614168014694217239" style="display:none">Marty Vail and the Psychopath. Bad boy lawyer Vail jams it up the governments ass sideways in a settlement, and is repaid by having to defend the accused in a viscous murder trial pro bono. As he peels the onion on Aaron Stampler, he finds that the boy is harboring deep psychological issues and upon further investigation finds that Aaron has a split personality, and that his alter ego is a satanic murderer. Facing the state that wants his client fried, Vail prepares and elaborate ruse to have the second personality come forward during intense cross examination at the trial, and the state is forced to settle the case of guilty but insane as the only alternative to a mistrial. Afterwards, as he awaits transport to the mental institution, Aaron reveals to Vail that he has been playing both sides against the middle, and he faked it all along.<br /><br />This had to be Diehl's crowning literary achievement; one hell of a read. The movie was scary enough, but couldn't bring out all of the details included in the book. For a reader who wants a spooky thriller that keeps you guessing ahead as to who's what. The two stars were cast magnificently for this movie by the way.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13326125303181936416">What a great book! This has become a new favourite of mine.<br/><br/>It moved at a fairly quick pace, but there were some things that I still skipped over. I really liked reading about the court case, but whenever there were segments that didn't pertain to the case I skipped them. I found they slowed down the pace of the book, and broke my focus on the bigger story (which could possibly have been the authors intention). Some parts I didn't find relevant.<br/><br/>That being said, I was glued to this book. No, I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText13326125303181936416" style="display:none">What a great book! This has become a new favourite of mine.<br /><br />It moved at a fairly quick pace, but there were some things that I still skipped over. I really liked reading about the court case, but whenever there were segments that didn't pertain to the case I skipped them. I found they slowed down the pace of the book, and broke my focus on the bigger story (which could possibly have been the authors intention). Some parts I didn't find relevant.<br /><br />That being said, I was glued to this book. No, I haven't seen the movie yet (but I now plan to!), and I think that helped me to enjoy the book more and keep focus instead of making comparisons to each version. I was intrigued by Aaron's character and the way he interacted with everyone. He understood what was going on, but was unable to articulate what he wanted to say. It was interesting to see his thought process.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I will read the other two in this series, but I highly recommend this book!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13326125303181936416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Vail has a good team to assist him with this case and uses unorthodox methods to get the information he needs.<br/><br/>Diehl built intriguing characters in an amazing story. Primal Fear had me wondering what Vail was going to do next in this enthralling legal suspense.<br/><br/>Stampler is a very gentle, mild mannered young man who claims he is innocent of killing the Bishop.   <span id="freeText7702310265204537962" style="display:none">Martin Vail is defending Aaron Stampler who is accused of murdering Archbishop Rushman. Vail has a good team to assist him with this case and uses unorthodox methods to get the information he needs.<br /><br />Diehl built intriguing characters in an amazing story. Primal Fear had me wondering what Vail was going to do next in this enthralling legal suspense.<br /><br />Stampler is a very gentle, mild mannered young man who claims he is innocent of killing the Bishop. However, when he is found hiding in the confessional covered in blood and holding the murder weapon, he looks guilty. I kept feeling like he didn't do it, so I was anxious to find out if he did or didn't.<br /><br />Diehl had a lot of technical mental health information in the book. This was necessary to understand the issues but, I must admit, it lost me several times along the way.<br /><br />The ending was a surprise and haunting.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14429461950074657701">Did not see this ending coming. Not since Orwell's 1984 has a last line in any novel chilled me the way Diehl's has. Far superior to any courtroom drama, "Primal Fear" employs the essential stream of suspense, but also tackles the psychological interior of criminal mind and motive. His style is blatant, sometimes crude; Diehl is not striving for poetic analogies or metaphors, but mostly dialogue, upbeat, fluid, and remarkably realistic. He uses this dialogue and characters with seemingly tangibl</span>
  <span id="freeText14429461950074657701" style="display:none">Did not see this ending coming. Not since Orwell's 1984 has a last line in any novel chilled me the way Diehl's has. Far superior to any courtroom drama, "Primal Fear" employs the essential stream of suspense, but also tackles the psychological interior of criminal mind and motive. His style is blatant, sometimes crude; Diehl is not striving for poetic analogies or metaphors, but mostly dialogue, upbeat, fluid, and remarkably realistic. He uses this dialogue and characters with seemingly tangible personalities to create a story of conflict, complications, denouement. And I applaud the denouement.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14429461950074657701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer990888545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3783250095716882049">A rippingly good suspense story with an addictive lawyer Vail and a chilling villain - or is he - in the form of Aaron. This is the second time I've read it and I did remember the plot and the outcome but it is such a well written book, it was still entertaining to read it for the second time. It was exciting, fast moving, had plenty of interesting characters and first time through - I remember my toes curling at the end. If you like dark psychological suspense stories - they don't get much bett</span>
  <span id="freeText3783250095716882049" style="display:none">A rippingly good suspense story with an addictive lawyer Vail and a chilling villain - or is he - in the form of Aaron. This is the second time I've read it and I did remember the plot and the outcome but it is such a well written book, it was still entertaining to read it for the second time. It was exciting, fast moving, had plenty of interesting characters and first time through - I remember my toes curling at the end. If you like dark psychological suspense stories - they don't get much better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3783250095716882049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JFHXEuC9Q1qjzT/Vfrlq7bggut77DduGSYiw63DWyzDqq5ywsK2U5uDnCLKpKLmRnv8qj9NVo3kdvOnAaD3W4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

In plain truth, Guevara says, “He’s like a kid (James Dean) I went to class with, rode the bus with and slid down an awesome snow-packed hill with.” And after high school, he goes on to Hollywood fame and immortality while Guevara from his modest bookish world is left to wonder about the iconic image, giving it a stark, poignant voice sixty years later. Guevara grew up in Marion, Indiana, where the actor was born. \n\nIn 1954, Dean met perhaps the one real romance of his brief life. Italian actress Pier Angeli was barely 22 when her movie The Silver Chalice coincided with Dean’s East of Eden at Warner Brothers. She’d sneak over to watch him perform, and he would do the same. When they finally interact, Pier’s mother disapproves of Dean’s behavior, attire and not being Catholic.\n\nSome say it was all for the limelight and publicity. Guevara’s gripping and frank story vies otherwise, excavating the actor’s true passion for the lovely but quaint Ms. Angeli.\n\nGuevara is also the author of True Feel, A Circle with Two Corners, and Days of Slint, the first James Dean conceptual novel.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5931880400212239929\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7052077053411790210">William Diehl was an American novelist and photojournalist.<br/><br/>Diehl was fifty years old and already a successful photographer and journalist when he decided to begin a writing career. His first novel, <i>Sharky's Machine</i>, which became a movie by the same name was directed by and starred Burt Reynolds. Diehl saw the movie shot on location in and around his hometown of Atlanta, Georgia. <br/><br/>Following the succ</span>
  <span id="freeText7052077053411790210" style="display:none">William Diehl was an American novelist and photojournalist.<br /><br />Diehl was fifty years old and already a successful photographer and journalist when he decided to begin a writing career. His first novel, <i>Sharky's Machine</i>, which became a movie by the same name was directed by and starred Burt Reynolds. Diehl saw the movie shot on location in and around his hometown of Atlanta, Georgia. <br /><br />Following the success of <i>Sharky's Machine</i>, Diehl relocated to St. Simons Island, GA in the early 80's where he lived for the next 15 years before going back to the Atlanta area. While living on St. Simons, he completed eight more novels, including <i>Primal Fear</i>, which also became a movie by the same name starring Richard Gere and Edward Norton. Diehl died at Emory University Hospital in Atlanta on November 24, 2006, of an aortic aneurism. He was a resident of Woodstock, Georgia at the time of his death and was working on his tenth novel.<br /><br /></span>
